\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00057}00057 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)f\$ u(x\_1,x\_2) \(\backslash\)f\$ as \(\backslash\)f\$ u(x\_i) \(\backslash\)f\$. We do not explicitly }}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00059}00059 \textcolor{comment}{context -\/-\/ in the above example it would be equal to the }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00060}00060 \textcolor{comment}{spatial dimension of the problem. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00061}00061 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00062}00062 \textcolor{comment}{All mathematical derivations are presented using}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00063}00063 \textcolor{comment}{the "{}natural"{} numbering of the indices: e.g., the components}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00064}00064 \textcolor{comment}{of the 3D vector \(\backslash\)f\$\{\(\backslash\)bf f\}\(\backslash\)f\$ are \(\backslash\)f\$ f\_1, f\_2 \(\backslash\)f\$ and \(\backslash\)f\$ f\_3 \(\backslash\)f\$.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00065}00065 \textcolor{comment}{Unfortunately, this notation is inconsistent with the }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00066}00066 \textcolor{comment}{implementation of vectors (and most other standard "{}containers"{})}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00067}00067 \textcolor{comment}{in C++ where the indices start from 0 and the components of }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00068}00068 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)c vector<double> \(\backslash\)c f(3) are \(\backslash\)c f[0], \(\backslash\)c f[1] and \(\backslash\)c f[2].}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00069}00069 \textcolor{comment}{There is no elegant way to resolve this conflict. Adopting C++-\/style}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00070}00070 \textcolor{comment}{numbering in the theoretical development would make the mathematics}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00071}00071 \textcolor{comment}{look very odd (try it!); conversely, adopting the "{}natural"{} }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00072}00072 \textcolor{comment}{numbering when discussing the C++-\/implementation would make this }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00073}00073 \textcolor{comment}{documentation inconsistent with the actual implementation.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00074}00074 \textcolor{comment}{We therefore use both numbering systems, each within their}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00075}00075 \textcolor{comment}{appropriate context.}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00552}00552 \textcolor{comment}{.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00553}00553 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00554}00554 \textcolor{comment}{For a "{}good"{} initial approximation, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00555}00555 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)f\$ U\string^\{(0)\}\_j\(\backslash\)f\$, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00556}00556 \textcolor{comment}{Newton's method converges quadratically towards the exact solution. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00557}00557 \textcolor{comment}{Furthermore, for linear}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00558}00558 \textcolor{comment}{problems, Newton's method provides the exact solution (modulo any}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00559}00559 \textcolor{comment}{roundoff errors that might be introduced during the solution of the }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00560}00560 \textcolor{comment}{linear system) in a single iteration. Newton's method can, therefore,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00561}00561 \textcolor{comment}{be used as a robust, general-\/purpose solver, if (!)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00562}00562 \textcolor{comment}{a good initial guess for the solution can be provided. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00563}00563 \textcolor{comment}{In practice, this is not a serious restriction,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00564}00564 \textcolor{comment}{because good initial guesses can often be generated by}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00565}00565 \textcolor{comment}{continuation methods. In \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib, Newton's method is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00566}00566 \textcolor{comment}{the default nonlinear solver. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00567}00567 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00568}00568 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00569}00569 \textcolor{comment}{Let us, briefly, examine the cost of the non-\/trivial steps involved}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00570}00570 \textcolor{comment}{in Newton's method: }}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00709}00709 \textcolor{comment}{  is symmetric only for certain types of basis functions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00710}00710 \textcolor{comment}{  This is not only advantageous for the solution of the linear}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00711}00711 \textcolor{comment}{  system (only a fraction of the entries in the matrix need to be computed,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00712}00712 \textcolor{comment}{  and (more efficient) linear solvers that exploit the symmetry }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00713}00713 \textcolor{comment}{  of the matrix can be used), but also properly reflects }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00714}00714 \textcolor{comment}{  the symmetry in the (self-\/adjoint!) ODE. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00715}00715 \textcolor{comment}{.}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00727}00727 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)section fe The Finite Element Method}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00728}00728 \textcolor{comment}{Galerkin's method is an efficient}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00729}00729 \textcolor{comment}{method for finding the approximate solution to a given problem if }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00730}00730 \textcolor{comment}{(and only if) we can:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00731}00731 \textcolor{comment}{-\/\# Construct a  function \(\backslash\)f\$ u\_p(x\_i) \(\backslash\)in H(D)\(\backslash\)f\$ }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00732}00732 \textcolor{comment}{   that satisfies the essential boundary conditions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00733}00733 \textcolor{comment}{-\/\# Specify a set of basis functions that}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00735}00735 \textcolor{comment}{   -\/\# vanishes on the domain boundary, and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00736}00736 \textcolor{comment}{   -\/\# leads to a sparse Jacobian matrix.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00737}00737 \textcolor{comment}{   .}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00738}00738 \textcolor{comment}{.  }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00739}00739 \textcolor{comment}{We shall now develop the finite element method: an}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00897}00897 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)subsection non\_uniform Improving the quality of the solution: non-\/uniformly spaced nodes and higher-\/order shape functions}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00898}00898 \textcolor{comment}{ Algorithm 2 presents the simplest possible}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00899}00899 \textcolor{comment}{ implementation of the finite element method for problem P1. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00900}00900 \textcolor{comment}{ We now discuss}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00901}00901 \textcolor{comment}{ two straightforward extensions that can significantly improve}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00902}00902 \textcolor{comment}{ the quality of the approximate solution.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00903}00903 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00904}00904 \textcolor{comment}{ The finite-\/element approximation in the previous section is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00905}00905 \textcolor{comment}{ piecewise linear between the nodal values. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00906}00906 \textcolor{comment}{ The accuracy to which the exact solution can be}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00907}00907 \textcolor{comment}{ represented by a piecewise linear interpolant is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00908}00908 \textcolor{comment}{ limited by the number of nodal points, which is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00909}00909 \textcolor{comment}{ the essence of the convergence statement (18). The }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00910}00910 \textcolor{comment}{ number of nodes required to resolve the solution to a given}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00911}00911 \textcolor{comment}{ accuracy depends on the nature of the }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00912}00912 \textcolor{comment}{ solution -\/-\/-\/ more nodes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00913}00913 \textcolor{comment}{ are needed to interpolate rapidly varying functions.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00914}00914 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00915}00915 \textcolor{comment}{ If the solution is rapidly varying in a small portion of the domain}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00916}00916 \textcolor{comment}{ it would be wasteful to use the same (fine) nodal spacing throughout}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00917}00917 \textcolor{comment}{ the domain. A non-\/uniform spacing, see below,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00918}00918 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)image html fe\_adaptive\_interpolant.gif "{}Adaptive 1D finite element mesh: Non-\/uniform spacing of nodes to achieve a high resolution only where it is required. "{} }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00919}00919 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)image latex fe\_adaptive\_interpolant.eps "{}Adaptive 1D finite element mesh: Non-\/uniform spacing of nodes to achieve a high resolution only where it is required. "{} width=0.75\(\backslash\)textwidth}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00920}00920 \textcolor{comment}{ improves the accuracy of the solution without greatly increasing}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00921}00921 \textcolor{comment}{ the total number of unknowns. Non-\/uniform spacing of the nodes }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00922}00922 \textcolor{comment}{ is easy to implement and does not require any significant changes }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00923}00923 \textcolor{comment}{ in Algorithm 2 -\/-\/ we simply choose }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00924}00924 \textcolor{comment}{ appropriate values for the nodal positions \(\backslash\)f\$ X\_j \(\backslash\)f\$; an }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00925}00925 \textcolor{comment}{ approach known as "{}h-\/refinement"{} because it alters the distance,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00926}00926 \textcolor{comment}{ \(\backslash\)f\$ h \(\backslash\)f\$, between nodes.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00927}00927 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00928}00928 \textcolor{comment}{<CENTER>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00929}00929 \textcolor{comment}{<TABLE class="{}oomph-\/table"{}>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00930}00930 \textcolor{comment}{<TR>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00931}00931 \textcolor{comment}{<TD class="{}panel panel-\/default"{}>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00932}00932 \textcolor{comment}{<CENTER class="{}panel-\/heading"{}>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00933}00933 \textcolor{comment}{<B> An aside: adaptive mesh refinement </B></CENTER>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00934}00934 \textcolor{comment}{<div class="{}panel-\/body"{}>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00935}00935 \textcolor{comment}{A non-\/uniform distribution of nodes requires a priori}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00936}00936 \textcolor{comment}{knowledge of the regions in which we expect the solution to undergo}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00937}00937 \textcolor{comment}{rapid variations. The alternative is to use adaptive mesh refinement: }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00938}00938 \textcolor{comment}{start with a }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00939}00939 \textcolor{comment}{relatively coarse, uniform mesh and compute the solution. If }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00940}00940 \textcolor{comment}{the solution on the coarse mesh displays rapid variations in certain }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00941}00941 \textcolor{comment}{parts of the domain (and is therefore likely to be poorly resolved), }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00942}00942 \textcolor{comment}{refine the mesh in these regions and re-\/compute. Such adaptive}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00943}00943 \textcolor{comment}{mesh refinement procedures can be automated and are }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00944}00944 \textcolor{comment}{implemented in \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib for a large number of problems; see the }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00945}00945 \textcolor{comment}{section \(\backslash\)ref example\_P2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00946}00946 \textcolor{comment}{for an example.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00947}00947 \textcolor{comment}{</div>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00948}00948 \textcolor{comment}{</TD>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00949}00949 \textcolor{comment}{</TR>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00950}00950 \textcolor{comment}{</TABLE>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00951}00951 \textcolor{comment}{</CENTER>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00952}00952 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00953}00953 \textcolor{comment}{ The quality of the interpolation can also be improved by }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00954}00954 \textcolor{comment}{ using higher-\/order interpolation, but maintaining}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00955}00955 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ the compact support for the global shape functions, so that}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00956}00956 \textcolor{comment}{  \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)psi\_j(x) \(\backslash\)f\$ is nonzero only in the vicinity of node}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00957}00957 \textcolor{comment}{  \(\backslash\)f\$ j \(\backslash\)f\$, and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00958}00958 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ the interpolation condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00959}00959 \textcolor{comment}{  \(\backslash\)f[  \(\backslash\)psi\_j(X\_i) = \(\backslash\)delta\_\{ij\} \(\backslash\)f]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00960}00960 \textcolor{comment}{  so that the shape function \(\backslash\)f\$ \(\backslash\)psi\_j \(\backslash\)f\$ is equal to one }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00961}00961 \textcolor{comment}{  at node \(\backslash\)f\$ j \(\backslash\)f\$ and zero at all others.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00962}00962 \textcolor{comment}{. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00963}00963 \textcolor{comment}{ For instance, we can use the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00964}00964 \textcolor{comment}{ (global) quadratic finite-\/element shape functions shown below:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00965}00965 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)image html 1Dmesh\_with\_quadratic\_shape\_fcts.gif "{}(Global) quadratic finite-\/element basis functions in 1D. "{} }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00966}00966 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)image latex 1Dmesh\_with\_quadratic\_shape\_fcts.eps "{}(Global) quadratic finite-\/element basis functions in 1D. "{} width=0.75\(\backslash\)textwidth}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00967}00967 \textcolor{comment}{ Note that we could also use shape functions with identical functional forms;}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00968}00968 \textcolor{comment}{ instead, we have chosen two different forms for the shape functions}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00969}00969 \textcolor{comment}{ so that the smooth sections of the different shape functions}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00970}00970 \textcolor{comment}{ overlap within the elements. This is not necessary but facilitates}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00971}00971 \textcolor{comment}{ the representation of the global shape functions in terms of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00972}00972 \textcolor{comment}{ their local counterparts within elements, see section \(\backslash\)ref local\_coords.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00973}00973 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00974}00974 \textcolor{comment}{ The implementation of higher-\/order interpolation does not}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00975}00975 \textcolor{comment}{ require any significant changes in Algorithm 2. We}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00976}00976 \textcolor{comment}{ merely specify the functional form of the (global) quadratic}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00977}00977 \textcolor{comment}{ finite-\/element shape functions sketched above.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00978}00978 \textcolor{comment}{ This approach is known as "{}p-\/refinement"{}, because it increases}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00979}00979 \textcolor{comment}{ order of the <B>p</B>olynomials that are used to represent the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00980}00980 \textcolor{comment}{ solution. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00981}00981 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00982}00982 \textcolor{comment}{<HR>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00983}00983 \textcolor{comment}{<HR>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00984}00984 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00985}00985 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00986}00986 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)section implementation An element-\/by-\/element implementation for 1D problems}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00987}00987 \textcolor{comment}{From a mathematical point of view, the development of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00988}00988 \textcolor{comment}{finite element method for the 1D model problem P1 is now complete, but }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00989}00989 \textcolor{comment}{Algorithm 2 }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00990}00990 \textcolor{comment}{has a number of features that would make it awkward to implement}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00991}00991 \textcolor{comment}{in an actual computer program. Furthermore, having been derived}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l00992}00992 \textcolor{comment}{directly from Galerkin's method, the algorithm is based on }}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02132}02132 \textcolor{comment}{The solution was computed with \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib, using a }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02133}02133 \textcolor{comment}{<A HREF="{}../../poisson/fish\_poisson/html/index.html"{}>driver code</A>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02134}02134 \textcolor{comment}{discussed elsewhere. Initially, the solution is computed on a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02135}02135 \textcolor{comment}{very coarse mesh which contains only four nine-\/node elements. Then }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02136}02136 \textcolor{comment}{the mesh is adaptively refined, guided by an}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02137}02137 \textcolor{comment}{automatic error estimator, and the problem is re-\/solved. This procedure}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02138}02138 \textcolor{comment}{is repeated several times. Note how the adaptation}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02139}02139 \textcolor{comment}{refines the mesh predominantly near the inward corners where the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02140}02140 \textcolor{comment}{solution has an unbounded gradient and is therefore (always) under-\/resolved.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02141}02141 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02142}02142 \textcolor{comment}{<HR>}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02145}02145 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02146}02146 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)section towards\_oo An object-\/oriented implementation}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02147}02147 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02148}02148 \textcolor{comment}{The steps described in Algorithm 10 can}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02149}02149 \textcolor{comment}{easily be implemented in a procedural language such as}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02150}02150 \textcolor{comment}{Fortran or C. The algorithm already contains}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02151}02151 \textcolor{comment}{a number of well-\/defined phases, which lend themselves to}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02153}02153 \textcolor{comment}{parameters (the number of nodes and elements, etc) and lookup schemes }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02154}02154 \textcolor{comment}{(the relation between local and global equation numbers,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02155}02155 \textcolor{comment}{the number of unknowns per element, etc.) generated}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02156}02156 \textcolor{comment}{during the setup phase would usually be passed to the subroutines}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02157}02157 \textcolor{comment}{(or functions) via common blocks (or }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02158}02158 \textcolor{comment}{<A HREF="{}http://c2.com/cgi/wiki?GlobalVariablesAreBad"{}>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02159}02159 \textcolor{comment}{(bad!) global data</A>). }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02160}02160 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02161}02161 \textcolor{comment}{We shall now discuss \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib's object-\/oriented implementation of the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02162}02162 \textcolor{comment}{finite-\/element method. We begin }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02163}02163 \textcolor{comment}{by examining the "{}objects"{} that occur}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02164}02164 \textcolor{comment}{naturally in algorithm 10 and aim to re-\/distribute}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02165}02165 \textcolor{comment}{all global data so that it becomes member data of an appropriate }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02166}02166 \textcolor{comment}{object. Three "{}objects"{} already feature prominently in many parts of }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02167}02167 \textcolor{comment}{our algorithms: }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02168}02168 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ the Nodes,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02169}02169 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ the Elements,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02170}02170 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ the Mesh.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02171}02171 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02172}02172 \textcolor{comment}{In the procedural version of the algorithm, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02173}02173 \textcolor{comment}{data associated with Nodes is }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02174}02174 \textcolor{comment}{stored in global arrays. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02175}02175 \textcolor{comment}{For instance, \(\backslash\)f\$ X\_\{ij\}\(\backslash\)f\$  stores the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02176}02176 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)f\$i\(\backslash\)f\$-\/th coordinate of global node \(\backslash\)f\$ j \(\backslash\)f\$; similarly, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02177}02177 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)f\$ U\_\{j\} \(\backslash\)f\$ stores the nodal value at }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02178}02178 \textcolor{comment}{global node \(\backslash\)f\$j\(\backslash\)f\$; etc. Nodal positions and values are accessed}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02185}02185 \textcolor{comment}{In \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib's object-\/oriented implementation, all nodal data is stored}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02186}02186 \textcolor{comment}{as member data of a Node object. Each Node stores}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02189}02189 \textcolor{comment}{.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02190}02190 \textcolor{comment}{as private member data. Access to these data }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02191}02191 \textcolor{comment}{is provided by member functions, e.g.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02192}02192 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)code}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02198}02198 \textcolor{comment}{[Note the C++ convention of starting indices at 0, rather than 1!]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02199}02199 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02200}02200 \textcolor{comment}{The Node object does \(\backslash\)b not store a node number! This is because }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02201}02201 \textcolor{comment}{node numbers are only used to identify Nodes in specific contexts. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02202}02202 \textcolor{comment}{For instance, as discussed above, the global node number identifies }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02203}02203 \textcolor{comment}{Nodes within the context of the global Mesh. Instead, we }}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02219}02219 \textcolor{comment}{\(\backslash\)f[ x\_i = X\_\{iJ(j\_\{local\},e)\}, \(\backslash\)f]}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02221}02221 \textcolor{comment}{that provides pointer-\/based access to its constituent Nodes}}

\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02227}02227 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02228}02228 \textcolor{comment}{Similar procedures can be implemented for all other objects. We use}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02229}02229 \textcolor{comment}{the general design principle that all objects store only their }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02230}02230 \textcolor{comment}{"{}own"{} intrinsic data and we replace all global lookup schemes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02231}02231 \textcolor{comment}{by pointer-\/based access functions. To guide the implementation, we}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02232}02232 \textcolor{comment}{observe the following inter-\/dependence between our three}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02233}02233 \textcolor{comment}{fundamental objects:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02234}02234 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02235}02235 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ \(\backslash\)b The \(\backslash\)b Nodes: Nodes have positions and values. The nodal values }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02236}02236 \textcolor{comment}{  are either "{}pinned"{} or "{}free"{}, in which case they }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02237}02237 \textcolor{comment}{  represent unknowns in the problem.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02238}02238 \textcolor{comment}{  The "{}pinned status"{} of a Node is indicated by its global equation }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02239}02239 \textcolor{comment}{  number, either a unique non-\/negative number, for unknowns, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02240}02240 \textcolor{comment}{  or -\/1, for values that are "{}pinned"{}. Note that this convention }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02241}02241 \textcolor{comment}{  makes "{}-\/1"{} a "{}magic number"{} -\/-\/ bad practice! In \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib, we}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02242}02242 \textcolor{comment}{  set the equation number of pinned Nodes to \(\backslash\)c Node::Is\_pinned -\/-\/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02243}02243 \textcolor{comment}{  a static data member of the Node class that is, in fact, set to -\/1.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02244}02244 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ \(\backslash\)b The \(\backslash\)b Elements: Elements contain Nodes and, within an Element,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02245}02245 \textcolor{comment}{  Nodes are identified by their local node numbers.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02246}02246 \textcolor{comment}{  Elements define their (local) shape functions and compute}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02247}02247 \textcolor{comment}{  the elemental residual vector and Jacobian matrix, using data }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02248}02248 \textcolor{comment}{  that is intrinsic to the Element. The entries in the Element's }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02249}02249 \textcolor{comment}{  residual vector and its Jacobian matrix are labelled by local }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02250}02250 \textcolor{comment}{  equation numbers, and each element stores a lookup scheme }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02251}02251 \textcolor{comment}{  for the correspondence between local and global equation numbers.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02252}02252 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ \(\backslash\)b The \(\backslash\)b Mesh: The Mesh consists of Elements and Nodes. The mesh }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02253}02253 \textcolor{comment}{  generation process defines the nodal positions and establishes }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02254}02254 \textcolor{comment}{  the connectivity between the Nodes. Meshes typically have a number }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02255}02255 \textcolor{comment}{  of boundaries and the Mesh defines which Nodes are located on which }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02256}02256 \textcolor{comment}{  boundary. Nodes are identified by a global node number within the Mesh.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02257}02257 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02258}02258 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02259}02259 \textcolor{comment}{An important difference between the three fundamental objects}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02260}02260 \textcolor{comment}{is the degree to which their member functions can be}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02261}02261 \textcolor{comment}{implemented in complete generality. For instance,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02262}02262 \textcolor{comment}{the Node object is completely generic -\/-\/ there is only one type of Node,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02263}02263 \textcolor{comment}{allowing the Node class to be fully implemented (as a "{}concrete class"{},}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02264}02264 \textcolor{comment}{in C++ terminology) in \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02265}02265 \textcolor{comment}{Conversely, although all Meshes have a certain amount of common functionality}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02266}02266 \textcolor{comment}{(e.g. they all provide pointer-\/based access to their constituent}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02267}02267 \textcolor{comment}{nodes), the implementation of other functions are Mesh-\/specific. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02268}02268 \textcolor{comment}{For instance, the Mesh generation process itself (typically }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02269}02269 \textcolor{comment}{performed in the Mesh constructor) depends on the domain geometry, the }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02270}02270 \textcolor{comment}{topology of its elements etc. Such functions must be implemented }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02271}02271 \textcolor{comment}{differently in different Meshes. \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib therefore provides an abstract}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02272}02272 \textcolor{comment}{base class \(\backslash\)c Mesh, which defines and implements all functions that}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02273}02273 \textcolor{comment}{are common to all Meshes. The class also defines a number of }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02274}02274 \textcolor{comment}{virtual functions to establish standard interfaces }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02275}02275 \textcolor{comment}{for functions that can only be implemented}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02276}02276 \textcolor{comment}{in a concrete (derived) class, such as \(\backslash\)c FishMesh.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02277}02277 \textcolor{comment}{The same principle applies to Elements which we endow with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02278}02278 \textcolor{comment}{a three-\/level inheritance structure:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02279}02279 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ The abstract base class \(\backslash\)c GeneralisedElement defines the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02280}02280 \textcolor{comment}{  common functionality that \(\backslash\)e all Elements must have.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02281}02281 \textcolor{comment}{  All Elements must have member functions that compute the elemental }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02282}02282 \textcolor{comment}{  Jacobian matrix and the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02283}02283 \textcolor{comment}{  elemental residual vector. The distinction }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02284}02284 \textcolor{comment}{  between \(\backslash\)c GeneralisedElements and \(\backslash\)c FiniteElements is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02285}02285 \textcolor{comment}{  useful because many elements in \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib are not finite elements, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02286}02286 \textcolor{comment}{  and, for instance, do not have nodes.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02287}02287 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ The abstract base class \(\backslash\)c FiniteElement is derived from }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02288}02288 \textcolor{comment}{  \(\backslash\)c GeneralisedElement and defines the common functionality}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02289}02289 \textcolor{comment}{  that is shared by all finite elements. The \(\backslash\)c FiniteElement class }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02290}02290 \textcolor{comment}{  implements all functions that are generic for finite elements}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02291}02291 \textcolor{comment}{  and specifies the interfaces for any remaining functions}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02292}02292 \textcolor{comment}{  that cannot be implemented in complete generality. For instance,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02293}02293 \textcolor{comment}{  all finite elements have shape functions but their implementation}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02294}02294 \textcolor{comment}{  depends on the geometry of the element.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02295}02295 \textcolor{comment}{-\/ Finally, we have concrete Elements that are derived from }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02296}02296 \textcolor{comment}{  \(\backslash\)c FiniteElement}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02297}02297 \textcolor{comment}{  and implement any virtual functions defined at lower levels; these}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02298}02298 \textcolor{comment}{  Elements provide a specific discretisation of a specific PDE. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02299}02299 \textcolor{comment}{  The \(\backslash\)c QPoissonElement<3,2> implements, inter alia, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02300}02300 \textcolor{comment}{  the computation of the element residual}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02301}02301 \textcolor{comment}{  and the element Jacobian matrix for the 2D Poisson equation,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02302}02302 \textcolor{comment}{  in a nine-\/node quadrilateral element. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02303}02303 \textcolor{comment}{  [\(\backslash\)b Note: In many cases, it is useful to sub-\/divide this}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02304}02304 \textcolor{comment}{  level further by introducing an intermediate class that}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02305}02305 \textcolor{comment}{  implements only the Element geometry;}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02306}02306 \textcolor{comment}{  motivated by the observation that a specific (geometric) Element type}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02307}02307 \textcolor{comment}{  (e.g. a 2D quadrilateral element) can form the basis for many different }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02308}02308 \textcolor{comment}{  concrete Elements, e.g. Elements that solve the Poisson, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02309}02309 \textcolor{comment}{  Advection-\/Diffusion or Navier-\/Stokes equations. Examples }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02310}02310 \textcolor{comment}{  of "{}geometric Elements"{} in \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib include the \(\backslash\)c QElements,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02311}02311 \textcolor{comment}{  a family of 1D line/2D quad/3D brick elements with}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02312}02312 \textcolor{comment}{  linear (or \{bi/tri\}linear), quadratic (or \{bi/tri\}quadratic),...}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02313}02313 \textcolor{comment}{  shape functions.]}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02314}02314 \textcolor{comment}{ }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02315}02315 \textcolor{comment}{ Algorithm 10 can easily be expressed in an }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02316}02316 \textcolor{comment}{ object-\/oriented }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02317}02317 \textcolor{comment}{ form because most steps involve operations that act exclusively }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02318}02318 \textcolor{comment}{ on the objects' member data. Such operations are }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02319}02319 \textcolor{comment}{ implemented as member functions of the appropriate objects.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02320}02320 \textcolor{comment}{ }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02321}02321 \textcolor{comment}{ The steps in  Algorithm 10 that do not }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02322}02322 \textcolor{comment}{ fall into this category (the application of }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02323}02323 \textcolor{comment}{ boundary conditions, setting of initial conditions and boundary values,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02324}02324 \textcolor{comment}{ etc) are usually problem-\/dependent and cannot be implemented }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02325}02325 \textcolor{comment}{ in generality. However, certain steps (e.g. the }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02326}02326 \textcolor{comment}{ solution of the nonlinear algebraic equations by Newton's method)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02327}02327 \textcolor{comment}{ are identical for all problems and should be implemented in a}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02328}02328 \textcolor{comment}{ general form. For this purpose, we introduce a fourth fundamental}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02329}02329 \textcolor{comment}{ object, \(\backslash\)b The \(\backslash\)b Problem, an abstract base class that provides}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02330}02330 \textcolor{comment}{ member functions for generic procedures such as}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02331}02331 \textcolor{comment}{ -\/ setting up the equation numbering scheme}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02332}02332 \textcolor{comment}{ -\/ solving the equations by Newton's method}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02333}02333 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02334}02334 \textcolor{comment}{ and stores}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02335}02335 \textcolor{comment}{ -\/ a pointer to the Mesh object}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02336}02336 \textcolor{comment}{ -\/ a vector of pointers to the unknowns which must be updated}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02337}02337 \textcolor{comment}{   during the solution of the nonlinear system by Newton's method.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02338}02338 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02339}02339 \textcolor{comment}{ Concrete problems, such as the \(\backslash\)c FishPoissonProblem discussed above,}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02340}02340 \textcolor{comment}{ should be derived from the abstract \(\backslash\)c Problem class. }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02341}02341 \textcolor{comment}{ Any problem-\/specific steps can }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02342}02342 \textcolor{comment}{ be implemented in member functions of the derived class, often the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02343}02343 \textcolor{comment}{ constructor.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02344}02344 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02345}02345 \textcolor{comment}{Here is an overview of overall data structure, as required by the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02346}02346 \textcolor{comment}{Poisson problems described above. The complete data structure}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02347}02347 \textcolor{comment}{implemented in \(\backslash\)c oomph-\/lib contains numerous extensions to permit the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02348}02348 \textcolor{comment}{solution of time-\/dependent problems, problems with many nodal values, }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02349}02349 \textcolor{comment}{problems in deforming domains, adaptive mesh refinement and many}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02350}02350 \textcolor{comment}{other features. A complete description of }}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02351}02351 \textcolor{comment}{<a href="{}../../the\_data\_structure/html/index.html"{}> the data}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\Hypertarget{intro_8txt__doxygenified_8h_source_l02352}02352 \textcolor{comment}{structure </a> is given elsewhere.}}
